<p>The <b>Rinkai Line</b> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">りんかい線</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Rinkai-sen</i><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span> is a railway line located in <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a>, Japan. It is the only line operated by the <a href="/wiki/Public%E2%80%93private_partnership#Japan" title="Public–private partnership">third-sector</a> company <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Waterfront_Area_Rapid_Transit" title="Tokyo Waterfront Area Rapid Transit">Tokyo Waterfront Area Rapid Transit</a>. It connects central Tokyo to the <a href="/wiki/Artificial_island" title="Artificial island">artificial islands</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aomi" title="Aomi">Aomi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Odaiba" title="Odaiba">Odaiba</a>. The line is served by some trains on the <a href="/wiki/East_Japan_Railway_Company" title="East Japan Railway Company">East Japan Railway Company</a> (JR East) <a href="/wiki/Saiky%C5%8D_Line" title="Saikyō Line">Saikyō Line</a> which continue on to <a href="/wiki/Shinjuku_Station" title="Shinjuku Station">Shinjuku</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ikebukuro_Station" title="Ikebukuro Station">Ikebukuro</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C5%8Cmiya_Station_(Saitama)" title="Ōmiya Station (Saitama)">Ōmiya</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kawagoe_Station" title="Kawagoe Station">Kawagoe</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rinkai_Line&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>While not part of the <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_subway" title="Tokyo subway">Tokyo subway</a> network (as it was built to JR specifications), the Rinkai Line is fully grade separated and runs underground for nearly 10 km of its 12.2 km distance, going as low as 40 meters below the ground when crossing under the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Tokyo" title="Port of Tokyo">Port of Tokyo</a>. The Shinonome – Shin-Kiba segment (which uses the former Keiyō Freight line) is elevated.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Station_list">Station list</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rinkai_Line&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Station list">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>All stations are located in <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a>. All trains stop at every station on the line.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rolling_stock">Rolling stock</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rinkai_Line&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Rolling stock">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Torin-train-base.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Torin-train-base.jpg/220px-Torin-train-base.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Torin-train-base.jpg/330px-Torin-train-base.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Torin-train-base.jpg/440px-Torin-train-base.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Torin-train-base.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Yashio Depot, January 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/TWR_70-000_series" title="TWR 70-000 series">TWR 70-000 series</a> 10-car EMUs (since 1996)</li>
<li>JR East <a href="/wiki/205_series" title="205 series">205 series</a> 10-car EMUs (2002-2016)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jrr2012_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-jrr2012-2">[2]</a></sup></li>
<li>JR East <a href="/wiki/E233_series#E233-7000_series" title="E233 series">E233-7000 series</a> 10-car EMUs (since 30 June 2013)</li>
</ul>
<p>The TWR 70-000 series <a href="/wiki/Electric_multiple_unit" title="Electric multiple unit">electric multiple unit</a> (EMU) trains are based at Yashio Depot, which is accessed via a spur located between Tennōzu Isle Station and Tokyo Teleport Station (the spur track also provides access to <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Freight_Terminal" title="Tokyo Freight Terminal">Tokyo Freight Terminal</a>), while the 205 and E233 series trains are based at Kawagoe Depot.</p>
<p>The first of a fleet of 31 new 10-car <a href="/wiki/E233_series#E233-7000_series" title="E233 series">E233-7000 series</a> sets were introduced on <a href="/wiki/Saiky%C5%8D_Line" title="Saikyō Line">Saikyō Line</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kawagoe_Line" title="Kawagoe Line">Kawagoe Line</a>, and Rinkai Line services between <a href="/wiki/Kawagoe_Station" title="Kawagoe Station">Kawagoe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shin-Kiba_Station" title="Shin-Kiba Station">Shin-Kiba</a> from 30 June 2013, displacing the fleet of 205 series EMUs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jreast20120410_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-jreast20120410-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-saitamashimbun20130607_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-saitamashimbun20130607-4">[4]</a></sup> As of February 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Rinkai_Line&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, one 205 series set, 28, remains in service while the E233-7000 series fleet undergoes modifications.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-railfan648_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-railfan648-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rinkai_Line&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Construction of the line started in 1992, with the eastern end of the line using the right-of-way of the Keiyō Freight Line (abandoned in 1983).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jrtr_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-jrtr-6">[6]</a></sup> The first portion of the line between <a href="/wiki/Shin-Kiba_Station" title="Shin-Kiba Station">Shin-Kiba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Teleport_Station" title="Tokyo Teleport Station">Tokyo Teleport</a> opened for service on March 30, 1996, initially under the name <b>Rinkai Fukutoshin Line</b> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">臨海副都心線</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Rinkai-fukutoshin-sen</i><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span>. The name was officially changed to the Rinkai Line on September 1, 2000. The extension to <a href="/wiki/Tenn%C5%8Dzu_Isle_Station" title="Tennōzu Isle Station">Tennōzu Isle</a> opened on March 31, 2001 and the final portion to Osaki on December 1, 2002.</p>
<p>The project ran severely over budget, with an estimated final cost of over ¥440 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jrtr_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-jrtr-6">[6]</a></sup> In 2005, the Rinkai Line's average ridership was 140,000 passengers per day<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jrtr_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-jrtr-6">[6]</a></sup> and, in 2006, the line finally registered its first operational profit, although interest payments on ¥389 billion yen in debt have resulted in a consistent net loss since 1991. By comparison, the competing elevated <a href="/wiki/Yurikamome" title="Yurikamome">Yurikamome</a> line is profitable, thanks to lower construction expenses, higher ticket prices and popularity among tourists and leisure visitors for its scenic views.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jrtr16_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-jrtr16-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>However, the Rinkai Line's ridership has steadily increased since, reaching 200,200 passengers per day in 2010. The ridership is forecast to increase further due to future development planned for the area served by the line.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Operating_company">Operating company</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rinkai_Line&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Operating company">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p><b>Tokyo Waterfront Area Rapid Transit, Inc.</b> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">東京臨海高速鉄道株式会社</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Tōkyō Rinkai Kōsoku Tetsudō Kabushiki-gaisha</i><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span> was founded on March 12, 1991 for the express purpose of constructing and operating the railway line. It is a <a href="/wiki/Public%E2%80%93private_partnership#Japan" title="Public–private partnership">third-sector</a> company, and, as of 1 April 2013, 91.32% of shares are held by the Tokyo Metropolitan Government, 2.41% by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JR_East" title="JR East">JR East</a>, 1.77% by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shinagawa,_Tokyo" title="Shinagawa, Tokyo">Shinagawa Ward</a>, 0.70% by <a href="/wiki/Mizuho_Bank" title="Mizuho Bank">Mizuho Bank</a>, 0.46% by <a href="/wiki/The_Bank_of_Tokyo-Mitsubishi_UFJ" title="The Bank of Tokyo-Mitsubishi UFJ">The Bank of Tokyo-Mitsubishi UFJ</a>, 0.34% by <a href="/wiki/Sumitomo_Mitsui_Banking_Corporation" title="Sumitomo Mitsui Banking Corporation">Sumitomo Mitsui Banking Corporation</a>, and the remaining 3% by 41 other companies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yahoo20140822_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-yahoo20140822-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>In spite of its severe financial situation, TWR was discovered to have made a five million yen donation to the <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Metropolitan_Government" title="Tokyo Metropolitan Government">Tokyo Metropolitan Government</a> on October 16, 2009 to encourage the city's <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_bid_for_the_2016_Summer_Olympics" title="Tokyo bid for the 2016 Summer Olympics">bid for the 2016 Olympic Games</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> The company stood to benefit financially if the games were held in Tokyo, as several of the proposed venues were located along the Rinkai Line.</p>
<p>In addition to its ownership and operation of the Rinkai Line, TWR is also involved in real estate and subcontracting/management of station- and building-related design.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_plans">Future plans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rinkai_Line&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Future plans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In August 2014, it was revealed that JR East was in negotiations to buy out the Rinkai Line.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yahoo20140822_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-yahoo20140822-9">[9]</a></sup> This would make it easier to incorporate the line into its plans for a direct line to <a href="/wiki/Haneda_Airport" title="Haneda Airport">Haneda Airport</a> as well as providing through services to and from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Keiyo_Line" title="Keiyo Line">Keiyo Line</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yahoo20140822_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-yahoo20140822-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
